<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft Foods Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>  Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>  (Unaudited)    <BR></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Accounting Policies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Basis of Presentation  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
interim condensed consolidated financial statements of Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), are unaudited. It is the
opinion of the Company's management that all adjustments necessary for a fair statement of the interim results presented have been reflected therein. All such adjustments were of a normal recurring
nature. Net revenues and net earnings for any interim period are not necessarily indicative of results that may be expected for the entire year. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>These
statements should be read in conjunction with the Company's consolidated financial statements and related notes, which are included in the Company's Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K
for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>On
November&nbsp;15, 2004, the Company announced the sale of substantially all of its sugar confectionery business for approximately $1.5&nbsp;billion. The transaction, which is subject to
regulatory approval, is expected to be completed in the second quarter of 2005. The Company has reflected the results of its sugar confectionery business as discontinued operations on the condensed
consolidated statements of earnings for all periods presented. The assets related to the sugar confectionery business were reflected as assets of discontinued operations held for sale on the condensed
consolidated balance sheets at March&nbsp;31, 2005 and December&nbsp;31, 2004. Accordingly, historical statements of earnings amounts included in the notes to the condensed consolidated financial
statements have
been restated to reflect the discontinued operation. In addition, the Company anticipates additional tax expense of approximately $270&nbsp;million to be recorded as a loss on sale of discontinued
operations in 2005. In accordance with the provisions of Statement of Financial Accounting Standards ("SFAS") No.&nbsp;109, the tax expense will be recorded when the transaction is consummated. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the fourth quarter of 2004, following the announcement of the pending sale of its sugar confectionery business, the Company realigned its North American segments. The Company's new segments,
which are reflected in these condensed consolidated financial statements and notes, are U.S. Beverages; U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; U.S. Convenient Meals; U.S. Grocery;
U.S. Snacks&nbsp;&amp; Cereals; Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The new segment structure in North America reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands
between segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors, to provide more focus on the separate beverage and grocery businesses, and to benefit from synergies in grain based
products. Historical data have been restated to reflect the new segment structure. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Stock-Based Compensation Expense  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company accounts for employee stock compensation plans in accordance with the intrinsic value-based method permitted by SFAS No.&nbsp;123, "Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation," which has
not resulted in compensation cost for stock options. The market value at date of grant of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock is recorded as compensation expense over the period of
restriction (three years). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005 and 2004, the Company granted shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock to eligible employees, giving them in most instances all of the rights
of shareholders, except that they may not sell, assign, pledge or otherwise encumber such shares and rights. Such shares and rights are subject to forfeiture if certain employment conditions are not
met. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005, the Company granted approximately 4.1&nbsp;million restricted Class&nbsp;A shares to eligible U.S.-based employees and also issued to eligible
non-U.S. employees rights to receive approximately 1.8&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A equivalent shares. The market value of the shares and rights granted to the Company's </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>9</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>employees
was approximately $196&nbsp;million, or $33.32 per restricted share or right, on the date of grant. Restrictions on the stock and rights lapse in the first quarter of 2008. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
fair value of the shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock at the date of grant is amortized to expense ratably over the restriction period. The Company recorded
compensation expense related to the restricted stock and rights of $38&nbsp;million and $25&nbsp;million for the quarters ended March&nbsp;31, 2005 and March&nbsp;31, 2004, respectively. The
unamortized portion, which is reported on the condensed consolidated balance sheets as a reduction of earnings reinvested in the business, was $337&nbsp;million at March&nbsp;31, 2005. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition to restricted stock, at March&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company had stock-based employee compensation plans that permit the issuance of stock options to employees. The Company applies the
recognition and measurement principles of Accounting Principles Board Opinion No.&nbsp;25, "Accounting for Stock Issued to Employees," and related Interpretations in accounting for stock options
within those plans. No compensation expense for employee stock options is reflected in net earnings, as all stock options granted under those plans had an exercise price equal to the market value of
the common stock on the date of grant. The following table illustrates the effect on net earnings and earnings per share ("EPS") if the Company had applied the fair value recognition provisions of
SFAS No.&nbsp;123 to measure stock-based compensation expense for outstanding stock option awards for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2005 and 2004: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
2004, the Financial Accounting Standards Board ("FASB") issued SFAS No.&nbsp;123 (revised 2004), "Share-Based Payment" ("SFAS No.&nbsp;123R"). SFAS No.&nbsp;123R requires companies to measure
compensation cost for share-based payments at fair value. The Company will adopt this new standard prospectively, on January&nbsp;1, 2006, and does not expect the adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;123R to
have a material impact on its consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Asset Impairment, Exit and Implementation Costs:</U>  </B></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Restructuring Program:  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program with the objectives of leveraging the Company's global scale, realigning and lowering its cost structure,
and optimizing capacity utilization. As part of this program, the Company anticipates the closing or sale of up to twenty plants and the elimination of approximately six thousand positions. From 2004
through 2006, the Company expects to incur up to $1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges, reflecting asset disposals, severance and other implementation costs, including $717&nbsp;million
incurred from January&nbsp;2004 through March&nbsp;31, 2005. Pre-tax restructuring program charges during 2005 are expected to be between $440&nbsp;million and $470&nbsp;million,
including $76&nbsp;million incurred in the first quarter of 2005. Approximately one-half of the pre-tax charges are expected to require cash payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Restructuring Costs:  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005 and 2004, pre-tax charges under the restructuring program of $57&nbsp;million and $279&nbsp;million, respectively, were recorded as asset impairment
and exit costs on the condensed consolidated statements of earnings. The first quarter 2005 pre-tax charges resulted from the announcement of the closing of two plants, for a total of
fifteen since January&nbsp;2004, and the continuation of a number of workforce reduction programs. Approximately $35&nbsp;million of the first quarter 2005 pre-tax charges will require
cash payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Pre-tax
restructuring liability activity for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2005 was as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Severance
costs in the above schedule, which relate to the workforce reduction programs, include the cost of related benefits. Specific programs announced during 2004 and the first quarter of 2005, as
part of the overall restructuring program, will result in the elimination of approximately 3,800 positions. Asset write-downs relate to the impairment of assets caused by the plant closings and
related activity. Other costs incurred relate primarily to contract termination costs associated with the plant closings and the termination of leasing agreements. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Implementation Costs:  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005, the Company recorded $19&nbsp;million of pre-tax implementation costs associated with the restructuring program, of which $15&nbsp;million was
recorded in cost of sales and $4&nbsp;million was recorded in marketing, administration and research costs on the condensed consolidated statement of earnings. These costs include the discontinuance
of certain product lines and incremental costs related to the integration of functions and closure of facilities. During the first quarter of 2004, the Company recorded $1&nbsp;million of
pre-tax implementation costs associated with the restructuring program. This charge was recorded in marketing, administration and research costs on the condensed consolidated statement of
earnings. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Asset Impairment Charges:  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
March&nbsp;2005, the Company reached an agreement to sell its fruit snacks business for approximately $30&nbsp;million. The transaction is expected to close in the second quarter of 2005.
The Company incurred a pre-tax asset impairment charge of $93&nbsp;million in the first quarter of 2005 in recognition of the pending sale of this business. The charge, which includes
the write-off of all intangibles associated with this business, was recorded as asset impairment and exit costs on the condensed consolidated statement of earnings. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005, the Company completed its annual review of goodwill and intangible assets and no charges resulted from this review. During the first quarter of 2004, the Company
recorded non-cash pre-tax charges of $29&nbsp;million related to an intangible asset impairment for a small confectionery business in the United States and certain brands in
Mexico. A portion of this charge, $17&nbsp;million, was reclassified to earnings from discontinued operations on the consolidated statement of earnings in the fourth quarter of 2004. The remaining
charge was recorded as asset impairment and exit costs on the consolidated statement of earnings. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Total:  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
pre-tax asset impairment, exit and implementation costs discussed above, for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2005 and March&nbsp;31, 2004, were included in the operating
companies income of the following segments: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Related Party Transactions:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
March&nbsp;31, 2005, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. owned 85.5% of the Company's outstanding shares of capital stock. Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.'s subsidiary, Altria Corporate Services,&nbsp;Inc.,
provides the Company with various services, including planning, legal, treasury, accounting, auditing, insurance, human resources, office of the secretary, corporate affairs, information technology,
aviation and tax services. Billings for these services, which were based on the cost to Altria Corporate Services,&nbsp;Inc. to provide such services and a management fee, were $71&nbsp;million
and $73&nbsp;million for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2005 and 2004, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
March&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company had short-term amounts payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. of $374&nbsp;million. Interest on these borrowings is based on the applicable London
Interbank Offered Rate. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;4.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Acquisitions:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, the Company acquired a U.S.-based beverage business for approximately $119&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
effect of this acquisition was not material to the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows in any of the periods presented. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;5.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Divestitures:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Discontinued Operations:  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>On
November&nbsp;15, 2004, the Company announced the sale of substantially all of its sugar confectionery business for approximately $1.5&nbsp;billion. The proposed sale includes the </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><I>Life Savers</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>,
</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Creme Savers</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Altoids</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>,
</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Trolli</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Sugus</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> brands. The transaction, which is subject to regulatory approval, is expected to be
completed in the second quarter of 2005. The Company has reflected the results of its sugar confectionery business as discontinued operations on
the condensed consolidated statements of earnings for all periods presented. Pursuant to the sugar confectionery sale agreement, the Company has agreed to provide certain transition and supply
services to the buyer. These service arrangements are primarily for terms of one year or less, with the </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>13</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Other:  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005, the Company sold its U.K. desserts business, its U.S. yogurt business and a minor trademark in Mexico. The aggregate proceeds received from sales of businesses during
the first quarter of 2005 were $190&nbsp;million, on which pre-tax gains of $116&nbsp;million were recorded. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
March&nbsp;2005, the Company reached an agreement to sell its fruit snacks business for approximately $30&nbsp;million. The transaction is expected to close in the second quarter of 2005.
The Company incurred a pre-tax asset impairment charge of $93&nbsp;million in the first quarter of 2005 in recognition of the pending sale of this business. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
operating results of the other businesses sold, discussed above, were not material to the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows in any of the periods
presented. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;7.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Contingencies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
and its subsidiaries are parties to a variety of legal proceedings arising out of the normal course of business, including a few cases in which substantial amounts of damages are sought. While
the results of litigation cannot be predicted with certainty, management believes that the final outcome of these proceedings will not have a material adverse effect on the Company's consolidated
financial position, results of operations or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Third-Party Guarantees:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At March&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company's third-party guarantees, which are primarily derived from acquisition and
divestiture activities, approximated $24&nbsp;million. Substantially all of these guarantees expire through 2013, with $8&nbsp;million expiring through March&nbsp;31, 2006. The Company is
required to perform under these guarantees in the event that a third party fails to make contractual payments or achieve performance measures. The Company has a liability of $19&nbsp;million on its
condensed consolidated balance sheet at March&nbsp;31, 2005, relating to these guarantees. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Non-amortizable
intangible assets consist substantially of brand names purchased through the Nabisco acquisition. Amortizable intangible assets consist primarily of certain trademark
licenses and non-compete agreements. Pre-tax amortization expense for intangible assets was $3&nbsp;million and $2&nbsp;million for the quarters ended March&nbsp;31, 2005
and 2004, respectively. Amortization expense for each of the next five years is currently estimated to be approximately $12&nbsp;million or less. </FONT></P>

<!-- ZEQ.=8,SEQ=16,EFW="2157556",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=738126,FOLIO='16',FILE='DISK016:[05CHI8.05CHI2468]DM2468A.;6',USER='MWEINST',CD=';6-MAY-2005;12:11' -->
<A NAME="page_dm2468_1_17"> </A>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft Foods Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;9.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Segment Reporting:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company manufactures and markets packaged food products, consisting principally of beverages, cheese, snacks, convenient meals and various packaged grocery products. Kraft manages and reports
operating results through two units, Kraft North America Commercial and Kraft International Commercial. Reportable segments
for Kraft North America Commercial are organized and managed principally by product category. Kraft International Commercial's operations are organized and managed by geographic location. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the fourth quarter of 2004, following the announcement of the pending sale of its sugar confectionery business, as discussed in Note&nbsp;5. </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><I>Divestitures</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, the Company realigned its North American
segments. Kraft North America Commercial's new segments are U.S. Beverages; U.S. Cheese,
Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; U.S. Convenient Meals; U.S. Grocery; and U.S. Snacks&nbsp;&amp; Cereals. Kraft International Commercial's segments are Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and
Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The new segment structure in North America reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer
sectors, to provide more focus on the separate beverage and grocery businesses, and to benefit from synergies in grain based products. Historical data have been restated to reflect the new segment
structure. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's management uses operating companies income, which is defined as operating income before general corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and
allocate resources. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze the business performance and trends of the various business segments. Interest and other
debt expense, net, and provision for income taxes are centrally managed and, accordingly, such items are not presented by segment since they are not included in the measure of segment profitability
reviewed by management. </FONT></P>

data were as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
discussed in Note&nbsp;2. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Asset Impairment, Exit and Implementation Costs</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, the Company recorded asset impairment, exit and implementation costs of
$169&nbsp;million and $292&nbsp;million during the first quarter of 2005 and 2004, respectively. See Note&nbsp;2 for a breakdown of these pre-tax charges by segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005, the Company sold its U.K. desserts business and recorded a pre-tax gain of $115&nbsp;million. This gain is included in the operating companies income of
the Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa segment. In addition, the Company sold a minor trademark in Mexico, resulting in a pre-tax gain of $1&nbsp;million. This gain is included in the
operating companies income of the Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;10.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Financial Instruments:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the quarters ended March&nbsp;31, 2005 and 2004, ineffectiveness related to cash flow hedges was not material. At March&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company was hedging forecasted transactions for
periods not exceeding the next fourteen months and expects substantially all amounts reported in accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses) to be reclassified to the consolidated statement of
earnings within the next twelve months. </FONT></P>

activities affected accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses), net of income taxes, as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;11.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Benefit Plans:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company sponsors noncontributory defined benefit pension plans covering substantially all U.S. employees. Pension coverage for employees of the Company's non-U.S. subsidiaries is
provided, to the extent deemed appropriate, through separate plans, many of which are governed by local statutory requirements. In addition, the Company's U.S. and Canadian subsidiaries provide health
care and other benefits to substantially all retired employees. Health care benefits for retirees outside the United States and Canada are generally covered through local government plans. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Other
expense, above, is due primarily to additional pension benefits related to workforce reduction programs under the Company's restructuring program. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Employer Contributions  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company presently makes, and plans to make, contributions, to the extent that they do not generate an excise tax liability, in order to maintain plan assets in excess of the accumulated benefit
obligation of its funded U.S. and non-U.S. plans. During the first quarter of 2005, approximately $200&nbsp;million and approximately $40&nbsp;million of employer contributions were
made to U.S. plans and non-U.S. plans, respectively. Currently, the Company anticipates making additional contributions of approximately $10&nbsp;million during the remainder of 2005 to
its U.S. plans and approximately $60&nbsp;million during the remainder of 2005 to its non-U.S. plans, based on current tax law. However, these estimates are subject to change as a result
of changes in tax and other benefit laws, as well as asset performance significantly above or below the assumed long-term rate of return on pension assets, or significant changes in
interest rates. During 2004, employer contributions of $299&nbsp;million and $254&nbsp;million were made to U.S. plans and non-U.S. plans, respectively. </FONT></P>

<TD WIDTH="3%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD COLSPAN=2 ALIGN="RIGHT"><HR NOSHADE SIZE=4></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE></DIV>
<!-- end of user-specified TAGGED TABLE -->


<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
December&nbsp;2003, the United States enacted into law the Medicare Prescription Drug, Improvement and Modernization Act of 2003 (the "Act"). The Act establishes a prescription drug benefit under
Medicare, known as "Medicare Part&nbsp;D," and a federal subsidy to sponsors of retiree health care benefit plans that provide a benefit that is at least actuarially equivalent to Medicare
Part&nbsp;D. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
May&nbsp;2004, the FASB issued FASB Staff Position No.&nbsp;106-2, "Accounting and Disclosure Requirements Related to the Medicare Prescription Drug, Improvement and Modernization
Act of 2003" ("FSP 106-2"). FSP 106-2 requires companies to account for the effect of the subsidy on benefits attributable to past service as an actuarial experience gain and
as a reduction of the service cost component of net postretirement health care costs for amounts attributable to current service, if the benefit provided is at least actuarially equivalent to Medicare
Part&nbsp;D. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company adopted FSP 106-2 in the third quarter of 2004. The impact for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2005 was a reduction of pre-tax net postretirement health care
costs and an increase in net earnings of $12&nbsp;million, which is included above as a reduction of $1&nbsp;million in service cost, $5&nbsp;million in interest cost and $6&nbsp;million in
amortization of unrecognized net loss from experience differences. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;12.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Credit Lines:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
March&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company's credit facilities included a $2.0&nbsp;billion, multi-year revolving credit facility expiring in July&nbsp;2006 and a $2.5&nbsp;billion,
364-day revolving credit facility expiring in July&nbsp;2005. In April&nbsp;2005, the Company's existing credit facilities were terminated and replaced by a new $4.5&nbsp;billion,
multi-year revolving credit facility that expires in April&nbsp;2010. The Company's new $4.5&nbsp;billion, multi-year revolving credit facility expiring in
April&nbsp;2010, which is for its sole use, requires the maintenance of a minimum net worth of $20.0&nbsp;billion, up from $18.2&nbsp;billion required in each of the previous facilities. At
March&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company's net worth was $30.1&nbsp;billion. The foregoing revolving credit facility does not include any other financial tests, any credit rating triggers or any
provisions that could require the posting of collateral. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;13.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Income Taxes:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>On
October&nbsp;22, 2004, the American Jobs Creation Act ("the Jobs Act") was signed into law. The Jobs Act includes a deduction for 85% of certain foreign earnings that are repatriated. The Company
may elect to apply this provision to qualifying earnings repatriations in 2005 and is conducting analyses of its effects. The U.S. Treasury Department recently provided additional clarifying language
on key elements of the provision, which is under consideration as part of the Company's evaluation. The Company expects to complete its evaluation of the effects of the repatriation provision within a
reasonable period of time. The Company does not expect the repatriation provisions of the Jobs Act to have a significant impact on its consolidated results of operations or its consolidated cash
flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Jobs Act also provides tax relief to U.S. domestic manufacturers by providing a tax deduction up to 9% of the lesser of "qualified production activities income" or taxable income. In
December&nbsp;2004, the FASB issued FASB Staff Position 109-1, "Application of FASB Statement No.&nbsp;109, "Accounting for Income Taxes," to the Tax Deduction on Qualified Production
Activities Provided by the American Jobs Creation Act of 2004"
("FSP 109-1"). FSP 109-1 requires companies to account for this deduction as a "special deduction" rather than a rate reduction, in accordance with SFAS No.&nbsp;109, and
therefore, the Company will recognize these benefits in the year earned. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Description of the Company  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
Foods&nbsp;Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), manufactures and markets packaged food products, consisting principally of beverages,
cheese, snacks, convenient meals and various packaged grocery products. Kraft manages and reports operating results through two units, Kraft North America Commercial and Kraft International
Commercial. Reportable segments for Kraft North America Commercial are organized and managed principally by product category. Kraft International Commercial's operations are organized and managed by
geographic location. At March&nbsp;31, 2005, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. held 98.0% of the combined voting power of Kraft's outstanding capital stock and owned 85.5% of the outstanding shares of
Kraft's capital stock. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>On
November&nbsp;15, 2004, the Company announced the sale of substantially all of its sugar confectionery business for approximately $1.5&nbsp;billion. The transaction, which is subject to
regulatory approval, is expected to be completed in the second quarter of 2005. The Company has reflected the results of its sugar confectionery business as discontinued operations on the condensed
consolidated statements of earnings for all periods presented. Accordingly, historical statements of earnings amounts included in Management's Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condition and
Results of Operations have been restated to reflect the discontinued operation. The assets related to the sugar confectionery business were reflected as assets of discontinued operations held for sale
on the condensed consolidated balance sheets at March&nbsp;31, 2005 and December&nbsp;31, 2004. In addition, the Company anticipates additional tax expense of approximately $270&nbsp;million to
be recorded as a loss on sale of discontinued operations in 2005. In accordance with the provisions of Statement of Financial Accounting Standards ("SFAS") No.&nbsp;109, the tax expense will be
recorded when the transaction is consummated. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the fourth quarter of 2004, following the announcement of the pending sale of its sugar confectionery business, the Company realigned its North American segments. Kraft North America
Commercial's new segments are U.S. Beverages; U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; U.S. Convenient Meals; U.S. Grocery; and U.S. Snacks&nbsp;&amp; Cereals. Kraft International
Commercial's segments are Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The new segment structure in North America reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands
between segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors, to provide more focus on the separate beverage and grocery businesses, and to benefit from synergies in grain based
products. Historical data have been restated to reflect the new segment structure. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
2004, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. announced that, for significant business reasons, the Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. Board of Directors is looking at a number of restructuring alternatives, including
the possibility of separating Kraft from the balance of Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. has indicated that continuing improvements in the entire litigation environment are a
prerequisite to such action by their Board of Directors, and the timing and chronology of events are uncertain. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
favorable net impact of asset impairment, exit and implementation costs on earnings and diluted EPS from continuing operations is due primarily to the following: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Restructuring Program</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;In January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program. As part of this program,
the Company anticipates the closing or sale of up to twenty plants and the elimination of approximately six thousand positions. From 2004 to 2006, the Company expects to incur up to
$1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges, reflecting asset disposals, severance and other implementation costs. During the first quarter of 2005 and 2004, the Company recorded
pre-tax charges of $76&nbsp;million and $280&nbsp;million, respectively, for the restructuring program, including pre-tax implementation costs of $19&nbsp;million and
$1&nbsp;million, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Asset Impairment Charges</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;During March&nbsp;2005, the Company reached an agreement to sell its fruit snacks business for approximately
$30&nbsp;million. The Company incurred a pre-tax asset impairment charge of $93&nbsp;million in the first quarter of 2005 in recognition of the pending sale of this business. The
transaction is expected to close in the second quarter of 2005. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>For further details on the restructuring program and asset impairment charges, see Note&nbsp;2 to the Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements and the Business Environment
section of the following Discussion and Analysis.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Gains on Sales of Businesses</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The favorable impact on earnings and diluted EPS from continuing operations is due primarily to the gain on
sale of the U.K. desserts business in the first quarter of 2005. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Lower Effective Income Tax Rate</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The Company's reported effective income tax rate decreased by 3.1&nbsp;percentage points to 28.7%, due
primarily to the resolution of outstanding items in the Company's international operations, as well as other benefits, including the impact of the domestic manufacturers' deduction under the American
Jobs Creation Act. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Currency</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The favorable currency impact on earnings and diluted EPS from continuing operations is due primarily to the weakness of the U.S.
dollar versus the euro, the Canadian dollar and certain other currencies. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Continuing Operations</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The decrease in results from continuing operations was due primarily to the following: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft North America Commercial, reflecting higher commodity and benefit costs and increased marketing spending, partially offset by favorable volume/mix and
higher pricing.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft International Commercial, reflecting higher commodity costs, increased marketing spending and higher infrastructure investment in developing markets,
partially offset by favorable volume/mix and higher pricing. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>For further details, see the Consolidated Operating Results and Operating Results by Business Segment sections of the following Discussion and Analysis.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Discussion and Analysis  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Business Environment  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company is subject to a number of challenges that may adversely affect its businesses. These challenges, which are discussed below and under "Forward-Looking and Cautionary Statements," include: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>fluctuations
in commodity prices;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>movements
of foreign currencies;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>competitive
challenges in various products and markets, including price gaps with competitor products and the increasing price-consciousness of consumers;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
rising cost environment;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
trend toward increasing consolidation in the retail trade and consequent pricing pressure and inventory reductions;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
growing presence of hard discount retailers, primarily in Europe, with an emphasis on own-label products;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>changing
consumer preferences, including diet trends;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>competitors
with different profit objectives and less susceptibility to currency exchange rates; and
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>concerns
and/or regulations regarding food safety, quality and health, including genetically modified organisms, trans-fatty acids and obesity. Increased government
regulation of the food industry could result in increased costs to the Company. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Fluctuations
in commodity prices can lead to retail price volatility and intense price competition, and can influence consumer and trade buying patterns. During the first quarter of 2005, the
Company's commodity costs on average have been higher than those incurred in the first quarter of 2004 (most notably dairy, coffee, meat, nuts, energy and packaging), and have adversely affected
earnings. For the first quarter of 2005, commodity costs had a negative pre-tax impact on the Company's consolidated results of operations of approximately $250&nbsp;million as compared
with the first quarter of 2004, which was partially offset by price increases. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
the ordinary course of business, the Company is subject to many influences that can impact the timing of sales to customers, including the timing of holidays and other annual or special events,
seasonality of certain products, significant weather conditions, timing of Company and customer incentive programs and pricing actions, customer inventory programs, Company initiatives to improve
supply chain efficiency, including efforts to align product shipments more closely with consumption by shifting some of its customer marketing programs to a consumption based approach, financial
situations of customers and general economic conditions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program, with the objectives of leveraging the Company's global scale, realigning and lowering its cost structure,
and optimizing capacity utilization. As part of this program (which is discussed further in Note&nbsp;2 to the condensed consolidated financial statements), the Company anticipates the closing or
sale of up to twenty plants and the elimination of approximately six thousand positions. From 2004 through 2006, the Company expects to incur up to $1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges,
reflecting asset disposals, severance and other implementation costs, including $76&nbsp;million and $280&nbsp;million incurred in the first quarters of 2005 and 2004, respectively. Total
pre-tax charges for the program incurred through March&nbsp;31, 2005 were $717&nbsp;million. Approximately one-half of the pre-tax charges are expected to
require cash payments. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>25</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=25,EFW="2157556",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=755002,FOLIO='25',FILE='DISK016:[05CHI8.05CHI2468]DS2468A.;11',USER='MWEINST',CD=';6-MAY-2005;12:09' -->
<A NAME="page_ds2468_1_26"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition, the Company expects to incur approximately $140&nbsp;million in capital expenditures from 2004 through 2006 to implement the restructuring program, including $19&nbsp;million spent in
the first quarter of 2005. From January&nbsp;2004 through March&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company spent $65&nbsp;million in capital to implement the restructuring program. Cost savings as a result of
the restructuring program were approximately $127&nbsp;million in 2004, are expected to increase by an incremental $120&nbsp;million to $140&nbsp;million in 2005, and are anticipated to reach
annualized cost savings of approximately $400&nbsp;million by 2006, all of which are expected to be used in supporting brand-building initiatives. Cost savings during the first quarter of 2005 were
approximately $57&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Acquisitions and Dispositions:  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>One
element of the Company's growth strategy is to strengthen its brand portfolios through a disciplined program of selective acquisitions and divestitures. The Company is constantly reviewing
potential acquisition candidates and from time to time sells businesses to accelerate the shift in its portfolio toward businesses&#151;whether global, regional or local&#151;that offer
the Company a sustainable competitive advantage. The impact of any future acquisition or divestiture could have a material impact on the Company's consolidated financial position, results of
operations or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>On
November&nbsp;15, 2004, the Company announced the sale of substantially all of its sugar confectionery business for approximately $1.5&nbsp;billion. The proposed sale includes the </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><I>Life Savers</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>,
</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Creme Savers</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Altoids</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>,
</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Trolli</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Sugus</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> brands. The transaction, which is subject to regulatory approval, is expected to be
completed in the second quarter of 2005. The Company has reflected the results of its sugar confectionery business as discontinued operations on the condensed consolidated statements of earnings for
all periods presented. The assets related to the sugar confectionery business were reflected as assets of discontinued operations held for sale on the condensed consolidated balance sheets at
March&nbsp;31, 2005 and December&nbsp;31, 2004. In addition, the Company anticipates that an additional tax expense of approximately $270&nbsp;million to be recorded as a loss on sale of
discontinued operations in 2005. In accordance with the provisions of SFAS No.&nbsp;109, the tax expense will be recorded when the transaction is consummated. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005, the Company sold its U.K. desserts business, its U.S. yogurt business and a minor trademark in Mexico. The aggregate proceeds received from sales of businesses during
the first quarter of 2005 were $190&nbsp;million, on which pre-tax gains of $116&nbsp;million were recorded. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
March&nbsp;2005, the Company reached an agreement to sell its fruit snacks business for approximately $30&nbsp;million. The transaction is expected to close in the second quarter of 2005.
The Company incurred a pre-tax asset impairment charge of $93&nbsp;million in the first quarter of 2005 in recognition of the pending sale of this business. The charge was recorded as
asset impairment and exit costs on the condensed consolidated statement of earnings. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
operating results of businesses acquired and sold, excluding the sugar confectionery businesses, were not material to the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash
flows in any of the periods presented. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
2004, the Company had operations and plants or sold product to third-party distributors located in 14 Middle East countries (as defined by the U.S. Department of State, Bureau of Near Eastern
Affairs), including a biscuit business acquired during 2003 in Egypt. In the region, the Company had operations and plants in three countries (Egypt, Morocco and through a majority owned joint
venture, Saudi Arabia). In addition, the Company sold products to third-party distributors located in 11 of these countries (Algeria, Bahrain, Israel, Jordan, Kuwait, Lebanon, Oman, Qatar, Tunisia,
United Arab Emirates and Yemen). Revenue generated from operations or sales to the third-party distributors in the Middle East was approximately $250&nbsp;million in 2004, representing 3.3% of the
net revenue of the Europe, Middle East and Africa segment. In addition, in 2004, the Company entered into agreements with third-parties for the resale of the Company's products into Iraq, Libya and
Syria. </FONT></P>

financial statements, during the first quarters of 2005 and 2004, the Company recorded asset impairment and exit costs of $150&nbsp;million and $291&nbsp;million, respectively, on its condensed
consolidated statements of earnings. During the first quarter of 2005 and 2004, the Company also recorded $19&nbsp;million and $1&nbsp;million, </FONT></DD></DL>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Gains on Sales of Businesses&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>During the first quarter of 2005, the Company sold its U.K. deseserts business and
recorded a pre-tax gain of $115&nbsp;million. This gain is included in the operating companies income of the Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa segment. In addition, the Company sold a
minor trademark in Mexico, resulting in a pre-tax gain of $1&nbsp;million. This gain is included in the operating companies income of the Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific segment. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
discussed in Note&nbsp;9. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Segment Reporting</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, the Company's management uses operating companies income, which is defined as operating income before
general corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors
analyze the business performance and trends of the various business segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Consolidated Results of Operations for the Three Months Ended March&nbsp;31, 2005  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discussion compares consolidated operating results for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2005 with the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 2.4%, due to the 2004 acquisition of Veryfine Products,&nbsp;Inc. ("Veryfine"). Excluding all acquisitions and divestitures, volume decreased 0.3%. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $484&nbsp;million (6.4%), due to higher volume/mix ($174&nbsp;million, including the shift in Easter timing from mid-April last year to late March this year),
favorable currency ($164&nbsp;million), higher net pricing ($119&nbsp;million, reflecting commodity-driven pricing, partially offset by increased promotional spending) and the impact of
acquisitions ($42&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of divested businesses ($15&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>28</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=28,EFW="2157556",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=869672,FOLIO='28',FILE='DISK016:[05CHI8.05CHI2468]DU2468A.;8',USER='MWEINST',CD=';6-MAY-2005;12:09' -->
<A NAME="page_du2468_1_29"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
income increased $184&nbsp;million (18.9%), due primarily to lower pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($141&nbsp;million), gains on the sale of businesses
($116&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($65&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($22&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher marketing, administration and research costs ($105&nbsp;million,
including higher benefit and marketing costs), unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($38&nbsp;million, due primarily to higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending) and the net
impact of higher implementation costs associated with the restructuring program ($18&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Currency
movements increased net revenues by $164&nbsp;million and operating income by $22&nbsp;million. These increases were due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro, the
Canadian dollar and certain other currencies. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's reported effective income tax rate decreased by 3.1&nbsp;percentage points to 28.7%, due primarily to the resolution of outstanding items in the Company's international operations, as
well as other benefits, including the impact of the domestic manufacturers' deduction under the American Jobs Creation Act. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Earnings
from continuing operations of $699&nbsp;million increased $149&nbsp;million (27.1%), due primarily to higher operating income and a lower effective income tax rate. Diluted EPS from
continuing operations, which was $0.41, increased by 28.1%. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
earnings of $713&nbsp;million increased $153&nbsp;million (27.3%). Diluted EPS from net earnings, which was $0.42, increased by 27.3%. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income increased $77&nbsp;million (9.2%), due primarily to lower pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($128&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix
($27&nbsp;million), higher pricing, net of unfavorable costs ($10&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending), lower fixed manufacturing costs
($6&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($5&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher marketing, administration and research costs ($86&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs) and the
2005 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program ($14&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft North America Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Beverages.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 12.5%, due primarily to refreshment beverages, partially offset by a decline in coffee. Refreshment
beverages volume increased, due primarily to a 2004 acquisition, partially offset by lower shipments in powdered soft drinks. In coffee, volume declined due to the impact on mainstream brands of
commodity-driven price increases, partially offset by growth in premium brand coffee. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>30</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=30,EFW="2157556",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=878016,FOLIO='30',FILE='DISK016:[05CHI8.05CHI2468]DW2468A.;8',USER='MWEINST',CD=';6-MAY-2005;12:09' -->
<A NAME="page_dw2468_1_31"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $61&nbsp;million (9.1%), due primarily to the impact of the 2004 acquisition ($34&nbsp;million), higher pricing, net of increased promotional spending ($19&nbsp;million,
reflecting commodity-driven pricing in coffee) and higher volume/mix ($8&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $6&nbsp;million (3.6%), due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs ($26&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher volume/mix
($5&nbsp;million), lower fixed manufacturing costs ($5&nbsp;million), higher pricing, net of unfavorable costs ($4&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and higher promotional spending)
and lower pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($4&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 0.3%, due primarily to gains in foodservice and cheese, partially
offset by lower shipments in Canada. Volume in the foodservice business increased, due primarily to the 2004 acquisition of the Veryfine beverage business and higher shipments to national accounts. In
cheese, volume also increased behind gains in natural cheese, cream cheese and processed cheese, benefiting from the shift in shipments supporting the Easter holiday. Volume declined in Canada, due
primarily to lower shipments of grocery products, ready-to-drink beverages and biscuits, primarily reflecting competitive initiatives. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $108&nbsp;million (6.3%), due primarily to higher pricing, net of increased promotional spending ($63&nbsp;million, reflecting commodity-driven pricing in late 2004),
favorable currency ($34&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($7&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions ($7&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income increased $48&nbsp;million (23.6%), due primarily to lower pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($48&nbsp;million), higher pricing, net of
unfavorable costs ($21&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending) and favorable currency ($5&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher marketing,
administration and research costs ($16&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), higher fixed manufacturing costs ($6&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs) and the 2005 implementation
costs associated with the restructuring program ($4&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Convenient Meals.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume was equal to prior year, as higher shipments in meats were offset by a decline in pizza. Meats volume
increased, driven by higher shipments of cold cuts and bacon. In pizza, volume declined, due primarily to increased competitive activity, partially offset by new product introductions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $42&nbsp;million (4.0%), due primarily to favorable net volume/mix ($26&nbsp;million) and higher pricing, net of increased promotional spending ($16&nbsp;million,
reflecting commodity-driven pricing in meats and pizza). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $6&nbsp;million (3.0%), due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs ($22&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), partially
offset by higher pricing, net of unfavorable costs ($9&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending) and lower pre-tax charges for asset impairment
and exit costs ($7&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Grocery.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 1.7%, due primarily to gains in enhancers and desserts. Enhancers volume increased, driven by spoonable
dressings, which were impacted by the shift in Easter timing, partially offset by a decline in salad dressings and barbeque sauces. In desserts, volume also increased, due primarily to higher
shipments of shelf-stable puddings and gelatins, and frozen whipped toppings, which benefited from the shift in Easter timing, partially offset by declines in sugar-free dry and
refrigerated packaged desserts. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues decreased $9&nbsp;million (1.5%), due primarily to higher promotional spending, net of higher pricing ($6&nbsp;million) and unfavorable volume/mix ($3&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $104&nbsp;million (49.1%), due primarily to higher pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($86&nbsp;million, including the
$93&nbsp;million asset impairment charge related to the pending sale of the fruit snacks business), unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($14&nbsp;million, driven by higher commodity costs)
and unfavorable volume/mix ($6&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Snacks&nbsp;&amp; Cereals.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 1.5%, as gains in biscuits and cereals were partially offset by a decline in salted snacks.
In biscuits, volume increased due primarily to gains in crackers and new product introductions in cookies. Cereals volume also increased due primarily to new product introductions. In salted snacks,
volume declined due to higher commodity-driven pricing on snack nuts. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $59&nbsp;million (4.6%), due primarily to higher volume/mix ($49&nbsp;million) and higher pricing, net of increased promotional spending ($10&nbsp;million, reflecting
commodity-driven pricing in snack nuts). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 0.3%, due primarily to the growth in developing markets, partially offset by the impact of divestitures and higher commodity-driven pricing on consumption growth. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $223&nbsp;million (9.8%), due primarily to favorable currency ($130&nbsp;million), favorable volume/mix ($87&nbsp;million) and higher pricing, net of increased promotional
spending ($17&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of divestitures ($12&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income increased $105&nbsp;million (55.9%), due primarily to the 2005 gains on sales of businesses ($116&nbsp;million), favorable volume/mix ($38&nbsp;million), favorable
currency ($17&nbsp;million) and lower pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($13&nbsp;million), partially offset by unfavorable costs and increased promotional spending,
net of higher pricing ($48&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($19&nbsp;million, including infrastructure investment in developing
markets) and higher fixed manufacturing costs ($5&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft International Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 1.2%, due primarily to growth in developing markets, including Russia, Ukraine and
the Middle East, partially offset by lower volume in Germany, following a price increase in coffee, and the divestiture of the U.K. desserts business in the first quarter of 2005. Beverages volume
increased, driven by higher refreshment beverage shipments in the Middle East and coffee shipments in Sweden, Russia and Ukraine, partially offset by lower coffee shipments in Germany following a
price increase. Cheese&nbsp;&amp; dairy volume also increased, benefiting from cream cheese promotions and new product introductions in the United Kingdom. In snacks, volume increased, as gains in
confectionery, benefiting from growth in Russia and Ukraine, were partially offset by lower biscuits volume in Egypt. Convenient meals volume declined, due primarily to lower promotions in Germany and
lower market performance in the United Kingdom. In grocery, volume also declined, due to the divestiture of the U.K. desserts business in the first quarter of 2005 and lower results in Germany and
Egypt. </FONT></P>

<A NAME="page_dw2468_1_33"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $175&nbsp;million (10.2%), due primarily to favorable currency ($121&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($64&nbsp;million), partially offset by increased promotional
spending, net of higher pricing ($5&nbsp;million) and the impact of divestitures ($5&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income increased $98&nbsp;million (63.2%), due primarily to the 2005 gain on the sale of the U.K. desserts business ($115&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($31&nbsp;million)
and favorable currency ($14&nbsp;million), partially offset by unfavorable costs and increased promotional spending, net of higher pricing ($51&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs) and
higher marketing, administration and research costs ($9&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume decreased 1.0%, due primarily to lower shipments in Brazil and China, partially offset by
growth in the Philippines. Snacks volume declined, impacted by increased biscuit competition in Brazil and China, partially offset by higher confectionery shipments in Brazil due to the shift in
Easter timing. Grocery volume also declined, due primarily to lower shipments in Venezuela. In beverages, volume declined, due primarily to increased refreshment beverage competition in Brazil and
China, partially offset by growth in the Philippines. Cheese&nbsp;&amp; dairy volume increased, due primarily to gains in the Philippines and new product introductions in Australia. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $48&nbsp;million (8.4%), due primarily to favorable net volume/mix ($23&nbsp;million) and higher pricing, net of increased promotional spending ($22&nbsp;million) and
favorable currency ($9&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of divestitures ($7&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income increased $7&nbsp;million (21.2%), due primarily to lower pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($11&nbsp;million), favorable volume/mix
($7&nbsp;million), higher pricing, net of unfavorable costs and increased promotional spending ($3&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($3&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher marketing,
administration and research costs ($10&nbsp;million, including increased marketing costs and higher infrastructure investment in developing markets) and higher fixed manufacturing costs
($7&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Financial Review</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Provided by Operating Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005, net cash provided by operating activities was $242&nbsp;million compared with $494&nbsp;million in the comparable 2004 period. The decrease in operating cash
flows is due primarily to higher pension contributions, an increase in cash payments associated with the restructuring program and higher inventory balances reflecting the higher cost for commodities. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Provided by (Used in) Investing Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>One
element of the growth strategy of the Company is to strengthen its brand portfolios through disciplined programs of selective acquisitions and divestitures. The Company is constantly reviewing
potential acquisition candidates and from time to time sells businesses to accelerate the shift in its portfolio toward businesses&#151;whether global, regional or local&#151;that offer
the Company a sustainable competitive advantage. The impact of future acquisitions or divestitures could have a material impact on the Company's cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005, net cash provided by investing activities was $55&nbsp;million, compared with net cash used in investing activities of $266&nbsp;million in the first quarter of
2004. This cash provided by investing activities in the first quarter of 2005 includes proceeds received from sales of businesses, whereas the cash used in investing activities in the first quarter of
2004 includes the purchase of a business. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005, the Company sold its U.K. desserts business, its U.S. yogurt business and a minor trademark in Mexico. During the first quarter of 2004, the Company acquired a U.S.
based beverage business. Capital expenditures for the first quarter of 2005 were $139&nbsp;million, compared with $148&nbsp;million in the first quarter of 2004. The Company expects
full-year capital expenditures to be slightly above full-year 2004 expenditures of $1.0&nbsp;billion, including capital expenditures required for the restructuring program.
These expenditures are expected to be funded from operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
previously discussed, during the fourth quarter of 2004, the Company announced the sale of its sugar confectionery business for approximately $1.5&nbsp;billion. This transaction, which is subject
to regulatory approval, is expected to be completed in the second quarter of 2005. In addition, in March&nbsp;2005, an agreement was reached to sell its fruit snacks business for approximately
$30&nbsp;million. This transaction also is expected to be completed during the second quarter of 2005. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>33</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>

<A NAME="page_dw2468_1_34"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Used in Financing Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2005, net cash used in financing activities was $366&nbsp;million, compared with $471&nbsp;million during the first quarter of 2004. The decrease in net cash used in
financing activities is due primarily to an increase in net borrowings, including amounts due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates, partially offset by an increase in the Company's
Class&nbsp;A share repurchases and dividend payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Debt
and Liquidity</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Debt.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company's total debt, including amounts due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates, was $12.7&nbsp;billion at
March&nbsp;31, 2005 and $12.5&nbsp;billion at December&nbsp;31, 2004. The Company's debt-to-equity ratio was 0.42 at March&nbsp;31, 2005 and December&nbsp;31, 2004.
The Company's debt-to-capitalization ratio was 0.30 at March&nbsp;31, 2005 and December&nbsp;31, 2004. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>34</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's new $4.5&nbsp;billion, multi-year revolving credit facility expiring in April&nbsp;2010, which is for its sole use, requires the maintenance of a minimum net worth of
$20.0&nbsp;billion, up from $18.2&nbsp;billion required in each of the previous facilities. At March&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company's net worth was $30.1&nbsp;billion. The Company expects to
continue to meet this covenant. The new, multi-year revolving credit facility does not include any other financial tests, any credit rating triggers or any provisions that could require
the posting of collateral. The new, multi-year revolving credit facility enables the Company to reclassify short-term debt on a long-term basis. At March&nbsp;31,
2005, in anticipation of the receipt of the proceeds from the sale of its sugar confectionery business, the Company did not reclassify any short-term debt as long-term debt.
The Company expects to refinance long-term and short-term debt from time to time. The nature and amount of the Company's long-term and short-term debt
and the proportionate amount of each can be expected to vary as a result of future business requirements, market conditions and other factors. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition to the above, certain international subsidiaries of Kraft maintain uncommitted credit lines to meet the short-term working capital needs of the international businesses. These
credit lines, which amounted to approximately $600&nbsp;million as of March&nbsp;31, 2005, are for the sole use of the Company's international businesses. At March&nbsp;31, 2005, borrowings on
these lines amounted to approximately $160&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Guarantees.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As discussed in Note&nbsp;7. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Contingencies</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, the Company had third-party
guarantees, which are primarily derived from acquisition and divestiture activities, of approximately $24&nbsp;million at March&nbsp;31, 2005. Substantially all of these guarantees expire through
2013, with $8&nbsp;million expiring through March&nbsp;31, 2006. The Company is required to perform under these guarantees in the event that a third party fails to make contractual payments or
achieve performance measures. The Company has a liability of $19&nbsp;million on its condensed consolidated balance sheet at March&nbsp;31, 2005, relating to these guarantees. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition, at March&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company was contingently liable for $138&nbsp;million of guarantees related to its own performance. These include surety bonds related to dairy commodity
purchases and guarantees related to the payment of custom duties and taxes, and letters of credit. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Guarantees
do not have, and are not expected to have, a significant impact on the Company's liquidity. </FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE ALIGN="CENTER" WIDTH="120">

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company believes that its cash from operations and existing credit facility will provide sufficient liquidity to meet its working capital needs, planned capital expenditures, future contractual
obligations and payment of its anticipated quarterly dividends. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Equity
and Dividends</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
repurchased 5.3&nbsp;million shares of its Class&nbsp;A common stock during the first quarter of 2005 at a cost of $175&nbsp;million. At March&nbsp;31, 2005, cumulative repurchases under
its previously announced $1.5&nbsp;billion authority totaled 6.7&nbsp;million shares of Class&nbsp;A common stock at an aggregate cost of $225&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
discussed in Note&nbsp;1. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Accounting Policies</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, during the first quarter of 2005, the Company granted approximately 4.1&nbsp;million restricted

Restrictions on the stock and rights lapse in the first quarter of 2008. The market value per restricted share or right was $33.32 on the date of grant. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Dividends
paid in the first quarter of 2005 and 2004 were $350&nbsp;million and $309&nbsp;million, respectively, an increase of 13.3%, reflecting a higher dividend rate in 2005, partially offset
by a lower number of shares outstanding as a result of Class&nbsp;A share repurchases. The present annualized dividend rate is $0.82 per common share. The declaration of dividends is subject to the
discretion of Kraft's Board of Directors and will depend on various factors, including the Company's net earnings, financial condition, cash requirements, future prospects and other factors deemed
relevant by Kraft's Board of Directors. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Market Risk</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company operates globally, with manufacturing and sales facilities in various locations around the world, and utilizes certain financial instruments to manage its foreign currency and commodity
exposures. Derivative financial instruments are used by the Company, principally to reduce exposure to market risks resulting from fluctuations in foreign exchange rates and commodity prices by
creating offsetting exposures. The Company is not a party to leveraged derivatives and, by policy, does not use financial instruments for speculative purposes. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2005 and 2004, ineffectiveness related to cash flow hedges was not material. At March&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company was hedging forecasted transactions
for periods not exceeding fourteen months and expects substantially all amounts reported in accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses) to be reclassified to the consolidated statement of
earnings within the next twelve months. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Foreign exchange rates.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company uses forward foreign exchange contracts and foreign currency options to mitigate its exposure to
changes in exchange rates from third-party and intercompany actual and forecasted transactions. Substantially all of the Company's derivative financial instruments are effective as hedges. The primary
currencies to which the Company is exposed, based on the size and location of its businesses, include the euro, Swiss franc, British pound and Canadian dollar. At March&nbsp;31, 2005 and
December&nbsp;31, 2004, the Company had foreign exchange option and forward contracts with aggregate notional amounts of $3.0&nbsp;billion and $2.9&nbsp;billion, respectively. The effective
portion of unrealized gains and losses associated with forward and option contracts is deferred as a component of accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses) until the underlying hedged
transactions are reported on the Company's consolidated statement of earnings. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Commodities.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company is exposed to price risk related to forecasted purchases of certain commodities used as raw materials by its
businesses. Accordingly, the Company uses commodity forward contracts as cash flow hedges, primarily for coffee, cocoa, milk and cheese. Commodity futures and options are also used to hedge the price
of certain commodities, including milk, coffee, cocoa, wheat, corn, sugar and soybean oil. In general, commodity forward contracts qualify for the normal purchase exception under SFAS No.&nbsp;133
and are, therefore, not subject to the provisions of SFAS No.&nbsp;133. At March&nbsp;31, 2005 and December&nbsp;31, 2004, the Company had net long commodity positions of $228&nbsp;million and
$443&nbsp;million, respectively. Unrealized gains or losses on net commodity positions were immaterial at March&nbsp;31, 2005 and December&nbsp;31, 2004. The effective portion of unrealized
gains and losses on commodity futures and option contracts is deferred as a component of accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses) and is recognized as a component of cost of sales in the
Company's consolidated statement of earnings when the related inventory is sold. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Forward-Looking and Cautionary Statements</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company and its representatives may from time to time make written or oral forward-looking statements, including statements contained in the Company's filings with the SEC, in its reports to
shareholders and in press releases and investor webcasts. One can identify these forward-looking statements by use of words such as "strategy," "expects," "plans," "anticipates," "believes," "will,"
"continues," "estimates," "intends," "projects," "goals," "targets" and other words of similar meaning. One can also identify them by the fact that they do not relate strictly to historical or current
facts. The Company cannot guarantee that any forward-looking statement will
be realized, although it believes that it has been prudent in its plans and assumptions. Achievement of future results is subject to risks, uncertainties, and the possibility of inaccurate
assumptions. Should known or unknown risks or uncertainties materialize, or should underlying assumptions prove inaccurate, actual results could vary materially from those anticipated, estimated, or
projected. Investors should bear this in mind as they consider forward-looking statements and whether to invest in or remain invested in the Company's securities. In connection with the "safe harbor"
provisions of the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995, the Company is hereby identifying important factors that could cause actual results and outcomes to differ materially from those
contained in any forward-looking statement made by or on behalf of the Company; any such statement is qualified by reference to the following cautionary statements. The Company elaborates on these and
other risks that it faces throughout this document, particularly in the "Business Environment" section preceding the discussion of operating results. It is not possible to predict or identify all risk
factors. Consequently, the following should not be considered a complete discussion of all potential risks or uncertainties. The Company does not undertake to update any forward-looking statement that
it may make from time to time. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Each
of the Company's segments is subject to intense competition, changes in consumer preferences and demand for its products, including diet trends, the effects of changing prices for its raw
materials and local economic and market conditions. Their results are dependent upon their continued ability to promote brand equity successfully, to anticipate and respond to new consumer trends, to
develop new products and markets, to broaden brand portfolios, to compete effectively with lower priced products in a consolidating environment at the retail and manufacturing levels and to improve
productivity. The Company's results are also dependent on its ability to consummate and successfully integrate acquisitions and to realize the cost savings and improved asset utilization contemplated
by its restructuring program. The Company may, from time to time, divest businesses that are less of a strategic fit within its portfolio, and its results may be impacted by either the gains or
losses, or lost operating income, from the sales of those businesses. In addition, the Company is subject to the effects of foreign economies, currency movements, fluctuations in levels of customer
inventories and credit and other business risks related to its customers operating in a challenging economic and competitive environment. The Company's results are affected by its access to credit
markets, borrowing costs and credit ratings, which may in turn be influenced by the credit ratings of Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. The Company's benefit expense is subject to the investment performance
of pension plan assets, interest rates and cost increases for medical benefits offered to employees and retirees. The Company's assessment of the fair value of its operations for purposes of assessing
impairment of goodwill and intangibles is based on discounting projections of future cash flows and is affected by the interest rate market and general economic and market conditions. The food
industry continues to be subject to recalls if products become adulterated or misbranded, liability if product consumption causes injury, ingredient disclosure and labeling laws and regulations and
the possibility that consumers could lose confidence in the safety and quality of certain food products. The food industry is also subject to concerns and/or regulations regarding genetically modified
organisms and the health implications of obesity and trans-fatty acids. Increased government regulation of the food industry could result in increased costs to the Company. </FONT></P>
